1509 : HW 27.7 |HW 27.7: gĕṇḍiṅ strī tĕpakan anūti kaṅsya-kaṅsyan (anūt a-?);  gĕṇḍiṅ, gaṇḍiṅ

1511 : HW 27.7 |HW 27.7: saṅ kili sira tâparĕk ri dewī / ācārī sira ri harĕp lawan karaṇḍan / wwantĕn lampuran aṅiduṅ lĕṅĕṅ swaranya;  lampur*
1512 : HW 27.7 |HW 27.7: saṅ kili sira tâparĕk ri dewī / ācārī sira ri harĕp lawan karaṇḍan;  ācārī
1513 : HW 27.7 |HW 27.7: wwantĕn lampuran aṅiduṅ lĕṅĕṅ swaranya / gĕṇḍiṅ strī tĕpakan anūti kaṅsya-kaṅsyan (r.: anūt akaṅsya-kaṅsyan?). Kaṅsi is an instrument used e.g. in battle and in the orchestra. Breasts are compared to it, so it may have been smallish and in shape like the modern bal. kaṅsi -- and two in number? It appears to have been the instrument of accompaniment par excellence, i.e. it may have provided the punctuation or rhythm.  kaṅsi
